# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Task: Kubernetes APF QueueSet Deep-Dive

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce an algorithmic deep-dive on APF QueueSet behavior, dispatch flow, and fairness tradeoffs.

## Scope

Focus on the APF QueueSet subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

The document has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here is a summary of what it covers:

---

**Structure of the document:**

1. **Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries** — clarifies that the QueueSet only handles admission/queuing/dispatching for already-classified requests; it does not classify them, authenticate callers, or run handler logic.

2. **Key Components** — explains each struct/interface with file citations:
   - `queueSetFactory` (two-phase construction)
   - `queueSet` (virtual-time state, counters, lock discipline)
   - `queue` (per-flow FIFO + `nextDispatchR`)
   - `request` (work model, `arrivalR`, `promise.WriteOnce` decision)
   - `requestFIFO` (doubly-linked list with O(1) remove and running `queueSum`)
   - `promise.WriteOnce` (cross-lock dispatch signaling)
   - `shufflesharding.Dealer` (entropy-efficient queue selection)
   - `WorkEstimate` / `SeatSeconds` (two-phase seat model, fixed-point arithmetic)
   - `configController` / `priorityLevelState` (lifecycle, borrowing statistics)

3. **End-to-End Flow** — four concrete steps traced through the actual code paths: classification → queue assignment → dispatch loop (FQSR virtual-finish criterion) → blocking wait → completion with deferred seat release and anti-windup adjustment.

4. **Failure Modes and Tradeoffs** — epoch overflow mitigation, rejection policy (AND gate on seats and queue depth), hardcoded 3 ms service estimate, anti-windup bound tradeoff, seat oversubscription stall, and graceful config change via queue attrition.

5. **Extension Points** — `promiseFactoryFactory`, `WorkEstimatorFunc`, borrowing via `lendablePercent`/`borrowingLimitPercent`, `QueueNoteFn`, and mandatory object guarantees.

6. **Operational Implications** — per-level mutex contention, O(queues) dispatch scan
... (truncated)

Creation, like\\n28: // config update, is done in two phases: the first phase consumes the\\n29: // QueuingConfig and the second consumes the DispatchingConfig.  They\\n30: // are separated so that errors from the first phase can be found\\n31: // before committing to a concurrency allotment for the second.\\n32: type QueueSetFactory interface {\\n33: \\t// BeginConstruction does the first phase of creating a QueueSet.\\n34: \\t// The RatioedGaugePair observes number of requests,\\n35: \\t// execution covering just the regular phase.\\n36: \\t// The denominator for the waiting phase is\\n37: \\t// max(1, QueuingConfig.QueueLengthLimit) X max(1, QueuingConfig.DesiredNumQueues).\\n38: \\t// The RatioedGauge observes number of seats occupied through all phases of execution.\\n39: \\t// The denominator for all the ratioed concurrency gauges is supplied later in the DispatchingConfig.\\n40: \\t// The Gauge observes the seat demand (executing + queued seats).\\n41: \\tBeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, metrics.RatioedGaugePair, metrics.RatioedGauge, metrics.Gauge) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\\n42: }\\n43: \\n44: // QueueSetCompleter finishes the two-step process of creating or\\n45: // reconfiguring a QueueSet\\n46: type QueueSetCompleter interface {\\n47: \\t// Complete returns a QueueSet configured by the given\\n48: \\t// dispatching configuration.\\n49: \\tComplete(DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\\n50: }\\n51: \\n52: // QueueSet is the abstraction for the queuing and dispatching\\n53: // functionality of one non-exempt priority level.  It covers the\\n54: // functionality described in the \\\"Assignment to a Queue\\\", \\\"Queuing\\\",\\n55: // and \\\"Dispatching\\\" sections of\\n56: // https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md\\n57: // .  Some day we may have connections between priority levels, but\\n58: // today is not that day.\\n59: type QueueSet interface {\\n60: \\t// BeginConfigChange starts the two-step process of updating the\\n61: \\t// configuration.  No change is made until Complete is called.  If\\n62: \\t// `C := X.BeginConstruction(q)` then `C.Complete(d)` returns the\\n63: \\t// same value `X`.  If the QueuingConfig's DesiredNumQueues field\\n64: \\t// is zero then the other queuing-specific config parameters are\\n65: \\t// not changed, so that the queues continue draining as before.\\n66: \\t// In any case, reconfiguration does not discard any queue unless\\n67: \\t// and until it is undesired and empty.\\n68: \\tBeginConfigChange(QueuingConfig) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\\n69: \\n70: \\t// IsIdle returns a bool indicating whether the QueueSet was idle\\n71: \\t// at the moment of the return.  Idle means the QueueSet has zero\\n72: \\t// requests queued and zero executing.  This bit can change only\\n73: \\t// (1) during a call to StartRequest and (2) during a call to\\n74: \\t// Request::Finish.  In the latter case idleness can only change\\n75: \\t// from false to true.\\n76: \\tIsIdle() bool\\n77: \\n78: \\t// StartRequest begins the process of handling a request.  If the\\n79: \\t// request gets queued and the number of queues is greater than 1\\n80: \\t// then StartRequest uses the given hashValue as the source of\\n81: \\t// entropy as it shuffle-shards the request into a queue.  The\\n82: \\t// descr1 and descr2 values play no role in the logic but appear\\n83: \\t// in log messages.  This method always returns quickly (without\\n84: \\t// waiting for the request to be dequeued).  If this method\\n85: \\t// returns a nil Request value then caller should reject the\\n86: \\t// request and the returned bool indicates whether the QueueSet\\n87: \\t// was idle at the moment of the return.  Otherwise idle==false\\n88: \\t// and the client must call the Finish method of the Request\\n89: \\t// exactly once.\\n90: \\tStartRequest(ctx context.Context, width *request.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}, queueNoteFn QueueNoteFn) (req Request, idle bool)\\n91: \\n92: \\t// Dump saves and returns the instant internal state of the queue-set.\\n93: \\t// Note that dumping process will stop the queue-set from proceeding\\n94: \\t// any requests.\\n95: \\t// For debugging only.\\n96: \\tDump(includeRequestDetails bool) debug.QueueSetDump\\n97: }\\n98: \\n99: // QueueNoteFn is called when a request enters and leaves a queue\\n100: type QueueNoteFn func(inQueue bool)\\n101: \\n102: // Request represents the remainder of the handling of one request\\n103: type Request interface {\\n104: \\t// Finish determines whether to execute or reject the request and\\n105: \\t// invokes `execute` if the decision is to execute the request.\\n106: \\t// The returned `idle bool` value indicates whether the QueueSet\\n107: \\t// was idle when the value was calculated, but might no longer be\\n108: \\t// accurate by the time the client examines that value.\\n109: \\tFinish(execute func()) (idle bool)\\n110: }\\n111: \\n112: // QueuingConfig defines the configuration of the queuing aspect of a QueueSet.\\n113: type QueuingConfig struct {\\n114: \\t// Name is used to identify a queue set, allowing for descriptive information about its intended use\\n115: \\tName string\\n116: \\n117: \\t// DesiredNumQueues is the number of queues that the API says\\n118: \\t// should exist now.  This may be non-positive, in which case\\n119: \\t// QueueLengthLimit, and HandSize are ignored.\\n120: \\t// A value of zero means to respect the ConcurrencyLimit of the DispatchingConfig.\\n121: \\t// A negative value means to always dispatch immediately upon arrival\\n122: \\t// (i.e., the requests are \\\"exempt\\\" from limitation).\\n123: \\tDesiredNumQueues int\\n124: \\n125: \\t// QueueLengthLimit is the maximum number of requests that may be waiting in a given queue at a time\\n126: \\tQueueLengthLimit int\\n127: \\n128: \\t// HandSize is a parameter of shuffle sharding.  Upon arrival of a request, a queue is chosen by randomly\\n129: \\t// dealing a \\\"hand\\\" of this many queues and then picking one of minimum length.\\n130: \\tHandSize int\\n131: }\\n132: \\n133: // DispatchingConfig defines the configuration of the dispatching aspect of a QueueSet.\\n134: type DispatchingConfig struct {\\n135: \\t// ConcurrencyLimit is the maximum number of requests of this QueueSet that may be executing at a time\\n136: \\tConcurrencyLimit int\\n137: \\n138: \\t// ConcurrencyDenominator is used in relative metrics of concurrency.\\n139: \\t// It equals ConcurrencyLimit except when that is zero.\\n140: \\tConcurrencyDenominator int\\n141: }\\n142: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/kubernetes--stripped@6d5678ae074d17945f174da2b064603131370a5f/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go\"}",

    "content": "1: /*\n2: Copyright 2019 The Kubernetes Authors.\n3: \n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\n7: \n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n9: \n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n14: limitations under the License.\n15: */\n16: \n17: package fairqueuing\n18: \n19: import (\n20: \t\"context\"\n21: \n22: \t\"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/debug\"\n23: \t\"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/metrics\"\n24: \t\"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request\"\n25: )\n26: \n27: // QueueSetFactory is used to create QueueSet objects.  Creation, like\n28: // config update, is done in two phases: the first phase consumes the\n29: // QueuingConfig and the second consumes the DispatchingConfig.  They\n30: // are separated so that errors from the first phase can be found\n31: // before committing to a concurrency allotment for the second.\n32: type QueueSetFactory interface {\n33: \t// BeginConstruction does the first phase of creating a QueueSet.\n34: \t// The RatioedGaugePair observes number of requests,\n35: \t// execution covering just the regular phase.\n36: \t// The denominator for the waiting phase is\n37: \t// max(1, QueuingConfig.QueueLengthLimit) X max(1, QueuingConfig.DesiredNumQueues).\n38: \t// The RatioedGauge observes number of seats occupied through all phases of execution.\n39: \t// The denominator for all the ratioed concurrency gauges is supplied later in the DispatchingConfig.\n40: \t// The Gauge observes the seat demand (executing + queued seats).\n41: \tBeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, metrics.RatioedGaugePair, metrics.RatioedGauge, metrics.Gauge) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\n42: }\n43: \n44: // QueueSetCompleter finishes the two-step process of creating or\n45: // reconfiguring a QueueSet\n46: type QueueSetCompleter interface {\n47: \t// Complete returns a QueueSet configured by the given\n48: \t// dispatching configuration.\n49: \tComplete(DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\n50: }\n51: \n52: // QueueSet is the abstraction for the queuing and dispatching\n53: // functionality of one non-exempt priority level.  It covers the\n54: // functionality described in the \"Assignment to a Queue\", \"Queuing\",\n55: // and \"Dispatching\" sections of\n56: // https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md\n57: // .  Some day we may have connections between priority levels, but\n58: // today is not that day.\n59: type QueueSet interface {\n60: \t// BeginConfigChange starts the two-step process of updating the\n61: \t// configuration.  No change is made until Complete is called.  If\n62: \t// `C := X.BeginConstruction(q)` then `C.Complete(d)` returns the\n63: \t// same value `X`.  If the QueuingConfig's DesiredNumQueues field\n64: \t// is zero then the other queuing-specific config parameters are\n65: \t// not changed, so that the queues continue draining as before.\n66: \t// In any case, reconfiguration does not discard any queue unless\n67: \t// and until it is undesired and empty.\n68: \tBeginConfigChange(QueuingConfig) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\n69: \n70: \t// IsIdle returns a bool indicating whether the QueueSet was idle\n71: \t// at the moment of the return.  Idle means the QueueSet has zero\n72: \t// requests queued and zero executing.  This bit can change only\n73: \t// (1) during a call to StartRequest and (2) during a call to\n74: \t// Request::Finish.  In the latter case idleness can only change\n75: \t// from false to true.\n76: \tIsIdle() bool\n77: \n78: \t// StartRequest begins the process of handling a request.  If the\n79: \t// request gets queued and the number of queues is greater than 1\n80: \t// then StartRequest uses the given hashValue as the source of\n81: \t// entropy as it shuffle-shards the request into a queue.  The\n82: \t// descr1 and descr2 values play no role in the logic but appear\n83: \t// in log messages.  This method always returns quickly (without\n84: \t// waiting for the request to be dequeued).  If this method\n85: \t// returns a nil Request value then caller should reject the\n86: \t// request and the returned bool indicates whether the QueueSet\n87: \t// was idle at the moment of the return.  Otherwise idle==false\n88: \t// and the client must call the Finish method of the Request\n89: \t// exactly once.\n90: \tStartRequest(ctx context.Context, width *request.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}, queueNoteFn QueueNoteFn) (req Request, idle bool)\n91: \n92: \t// Dump saves and returns the instant internal state of the queue-set.\n93: \t// Note that dumping process will stop the queue-set from proceeding\n94: \t// any requests.\n95: \t// For debugging only.\n96: \tDump(includeRequestDetails bool) debug.QueueSetDump\n97: }\n98: \n99: // QueueNoteFn is called when a request enters and leaves a queue\n100: type QueueNoteFn func(inQueue bool)\n101: \n102: // Request represents the remainder of the handling of one request\n103: type Request interface {\n104: \t// Finish determines whether to execute or reject the request and\n105: \t// invokes `execute` if the decision is to execute the request.\n106: \t// The returned `idle bool` value indicates whether the QueueSet\n107: \t// was idle when the value was calculated, but might no longer be\n108: \t// accurate by the time the client examines that value.\n109: \tFinish(execute func()) (idle bool)\n110: }\n111: \n112: // QueuingConfig defines the configuration of the queuing aspect of a QueueSet.\n113: type QueuingConfig struct {\n114: \t// Name is used to identify a queue set, allowing for descriptive information about its intended use\n115: \tName string\n116: \n117: \t// DesiredNumQueues is the number of queues that the API says\n118: \t// should exist now. Thus, it should be invoked after acquiring the\\n464: // lock and before modifying the state of any queue.\\n465: func (qs *queueSet) syncTimeLocked(ctx context.Context) {\\n466: \\trealNow := fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds / 2\\n484: \\n485: // highR is the threshold that triggers advance of the epoch.\\n486: // That is, decrementing the global progress meter R by rDecrement.\\n487: const highR and incrR parameters are only used to add info to the log messages.\\n492: func (qs *queueSet) advanceEpoch(ctx context.Context, now time.Time, incrR fqrequest.SeatSeconds) {\\n493: \\toldR := }\\n523: \\n524: // getVirtualTimeRatio calculates the rate at which virtual time has\\n525: // been advancing, according to the logic in `doc.go`.\\n526: func (qs *queueSet) The fields listed before the lock\n71: // should not be changed; the fields listed after the\n72: // lock must be accessed only while holding the lock.\n73: //\n74: // The methods of this type follow the naming convention that the\n75: // suffix \"Locked\" means the caller must hold the lock; for a method\n76: // whose name does not end in \"Locked\" either acquires the lock or\n77: // does not care about locking.\n78: //\n79: // The methods of this type also follow the convention that the suffix\n80: // \"ToBoundLocked\" means that the caller may have to follow up with a\n81: // call to `boundNextDispatchLocked`.  This is so for a method that\n82: // changes what request is oldest in a queue, because that change means\n83: // that the anti-windup hack in boundNextDispatchLocked needs to be\n84: // applied wrt the revised oldest request in the queue.\n85: type queueSet struct {\n86: \tclock                    eventclock.Interface\n87: \testimatedServiceDuration time.Duration\n88: \n89: \treqsGaugePair metrics.RatioedGaugePair // .RequestsExecuting covers regular phase only\n90: \n91: \texecSeatsGauge metrics.RatioedGauge // for all phases of execution\n92: \n93: \tseatDemandIntegrator metrics.Gauge\n94: \n95: \tpromiseFactory promiseFactory\n96: \n97: \tlock sync.Mutex\n98: \n99: \t// qCfg holds the current queuing configuration.                c,\n178: \t\tpromiseFactoryFactory: promiseFactoryFactory,\n179: \t}\n180: }\n181: \n182: func (qsf *queueSetFactory) BeginConstruction(qCfg fq.QueuingConfig, reqsGaugePair dealer, err\n208: }\n209: \n210: func (qsc *queueSetCompleter) Complete(dCfg fq.DispatchingConfig) fq.QueueSet {\n211: \tqs := qsc.theSet\n212: \tif qs == nil {\n213: \t\tqs = &queueSet{\n214: \t\t\tclock:                    qsc.factory.clock,\n215: \t\t\testimatedServiceDuration: 3 * time.Millisecond,\n216: \t\t\treqsGaugePair:            qsc.reqsGaugePair,\n217: \t\t\texecSeatsGauge:           qsc.execSeatsGauge,\n218: \t\t\tseatDemandIntegrator:     qsc.seatDemandIntegrator,\n219: \t\t\tqCfg:                     qsc.qCfg,\n220: \t\t\tcurrentR:                 0,\n221: for initializing an array of n queues\n231: func createQueues(n, baseIndex int) []*queue {\n232: \tfqqueues := make([]*queue, n)\n233: \tfor i := 0; i < n; i++ {\n234: \t\tfqqueues[i] = &queue{index: fq.QueuingConfig) (fq.QueueSetCompleter, error) {\n240: \tdealer, err := checkConfig(qCfg)\n241: \tif err != nil {\n242: \t\treturn nil, err\n243: \t}\n244: \treturn &queueSetCompleter{\n245: \t\ttheSet: qs,\n246: \t\tqCfg:   qCfg,\n247: \t\tdealer: dealer}, nil\n248: }\n249: \n250: // setConfiguration is used to set the configuration for a queueSet.\n251: // Update handling for when fields are updated is handled here as well -\n252: // eg: if DesiredNum is increased, setConfiguration reconciles by\n253: // adding more queues.\n254: func (qs *queueSet) setConfiguration(ctx context.Context, qCfg fq.QueuingConfig, dealer *shufflesharding.Dealer, dCfg fq.DispatchingConfig) {\n255: \tqs.lockAndSyncTime(ctx)\n256: \tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n257: \n258: \tif qCfg.DesiredNumQueues > 0 {\n259: \t\t// Adding queues is the only thing that requires immediate action\n260: \t\t// Removing queues is handled by attrition, removing a queue when\n261: \t\t// it goes empty and there are too many.\n262: \t\tnumQueues := len(qs.queues)\n263: \t\tif qCfg.DesiredNumQueues > numQueues {\n264: \t\t\tqs.queues = append(qs.queues,\n265: qs.qCfg.HandSize\n270: \t}\n271: \n272: \tqs.qCfg = qCfg\n273: \tqs.dCfg = dCfg\n274: \tqs.dealer = dealer\n275: \tqll := qCfg.QueueLengthLimit\n276: \tif qll < 1 {\n277: \t\tqll = 1\n278: \t}\n279: \tif qCfg.DesiredNumQueues > 0 {\n280: \t\tqll *= qCfg.DesiredNumQueues\n281: \t}\n282: \tqs.reqsGaugePair.RequestsWaiting.SetDenominator(float64(qll))\n283: \tqs.reqsGaugePair.RequestsExecuting.SetDenominator(float64(dCfg.ConcurrencyDenominator))\n284: \tqs.execSeatsGauge.SetDenominator(float64(dCfg.ConcurrencyDenominator))\n285: \n286: \tqs.dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n287: }\n288: \n289: // A decision about a request\n290: type requestDecision int\n291: \n292: // Values passed through a request's decision\n293: const (\n294: \t// Serve this one\n295: \tdecisionExecute requestDecision = iota\n296: \n297: \t// This one's context timed out / was canceled\n298: \tdecisionCancel\n299: )\n300: \n301: // StartRequest begins the process of handling a request.  We take the\n302: // approach of updating the metrics about total requests queued and\n303: // executing at each point where there is a change in that quantity,\n304: // because the metrics --- and only the metrics --- track that\n305: // quantity per FlowSchema.\n306: // The queueSet's promiseFactory is invoked once if the returned Request is non-nil,\n307: // not invoked if the Request is nil.\n308: func (qs *queueSet) StartRequest(ctx context.Context, workEstimate *fqrequest.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}, queueNoteFn fq.QueueNoteFn) (fq.Request, bool) {\n309: \tqs.lockAndSyncTime(ctx)\n310: \tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n311: \tvar req *request\n312: \n313: \t// ========================================================================\n314: \t// Step 0:\n315: \t// Apply only concurrency limit, if zero queues desired\n316: \tif qs.qCfg.DesiredNumQueues < 1 {\n317: \t\tif !qs.canAccommodateSeatsLocked(workEstimate.MaxSeats()) {\n318: \t\t\tklog.V(5).Infof(\"QS(%s): rejecting request %q %#+v %#+v because %d seats are asked for, %d seats are in use (%d are executing) and the limit is %d\",\n319: \t\t\t\tqs.qCfg.Name, fsName, descr1, descr2, workEstimate, qs.totSeatsInUse, qs.totRequestsExecuting, qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)\n320: \t\t\tqs.totRequestsRejected++\n321: \t\t\tmetrics.AddReject(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, \"concurrency-limit\")\n322: \t\t\treturn nil, qs.isIdleLocked()\n323: \t\t}\n324: \t\treq = qs.dispatchSansQueueLocked(ctx, workEstimate, flowDistinguisher, fsName, descr1, descr2)\n325: \t\treturn req, false\n326: \t}\n327: \n328: \t// ========================================================================\n329: \t// Step 1:\n330: \t// 1) Start with shuffle sharding, to pick a queue.\n331: \t// 2) Reject current request if there is not enough concurrency shares and\n332: \t// we are at max queue length\n333: \t// 3) If not rejected, create a request and enqueue\n334: \treq = qs.shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked(ctx, workEstimate, hashValue, flowDistinguisher, fsName, descr1, descr2, queueNoteFn)\n335: \t// req == nil means that the request was rejected - no remaining\n336: \t// concurrency shares and at max queue length already\n337: \tif req == nil {\n338: \t\tklog.V(5).Infof(\"QS(%s): rejecting request %q %#+v %#+v due to queue full\", qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, descr1, descr2)\n339: \t\tqs.totRequestsRejected++\n340: \t\tmetrics.AddReject(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, \"queue-full\")\n341: \t\treturn nil, qs.isIdleLocked()\n342: \t}\n343: \n344: \t// ========================================================================\n345: \t// Step 2:\n346: \t// The next step is to invoke the method that dequeues as much\n347: \t// as possible.\n348: \t// This method runs a loop, as long as there are non-empty\n349: \t// queues and the number currently executing is less than the\n350: \t// assured concurrency value.  The body of the loop uses the\n351: \t// fair queuing technique to pick a queue and dispatch a\n352: \t// request from that queue.\n353: \tqs.dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n354: \n355: \treturn req, false\n356: }\n357: \n358: // ordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory is the promiseFactoryFactory that\n359: // a queueSetFactory would ordinarily use.\n360: // Test code might use something different.\n361: func ordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory(qs *queueSet) promiseFactory {\n362: \treturn promise.NewWriteOnce\n363: }\n364: \n365: // MaxSeats returns the maximum number of seats this request requires, it is\n366: // the maxumum of the two - WorkEstimate.InitialSeats, WorkEstimate.FinalSeats.\n367: func (req *request) MaxSeats() int {\n368: \treturn req.workEstimate.MaxSeats()\n369: }\n370: \n371: func (req *request) InitialSeats() int {\n372: \treturn int(req.workEstimate.InitialSeats)\n373: }\n374: \n375: func (req *request) NoteQueued(inQueue bool) {\n376: \tif req.queueNoteFn != nil {\n377: \t\treq.queueNoteFn(inQueue)\n378: \t}\n379: }\n380: \n381: func (req *request) Finish(execFn func()) bool {\n382: \texec, idle := req.wait()\n383: \tif !exec {\n384: \t\treturn idle\n385: \t}\n386: \tfunc() {\n387: \t\tdefer func() {\n388: \t\t\tidle = req.qs.finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible(req)\n389: \t\t}()\n390: \n391: \t\texecFn()\n392: \t}()\n393: \n394: \treturn idle\n395: }\n396: \n397: func (req *request) wait() (bool, bool) {\n398: \tqs := req.qs\n399: \n400: \t// ========================================================================\n401: \t// Step 3:\n402: \t// The final step is to wait on a decision from\n403: \t// somewhere and then act on it.\n404: \tdecisionAny := req.decision.Get()\n405: \tqs.lockAndSyncTime(req.ctx)\n406: \tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n407: \tif req.waitStarted {\n408: \t\t// This can not happen, because the client is forbidden to\n409: \t\t// call Wait twice on the same request\n410: \t\tklog.Errorf(\"Duplicate call to the Wait method!  Immediately returning execute=false.  QueueSet=%s, startTime=%s, descr1=%#+v, descr2=%#+v\", req.qs.qCfg.Name, req.startTime, req.descr1, req.descr2)\n411: \t\treturn false, qs.isIdleLocked()\n412: \t}\n413: \treq.waitStarted = true\n414: \tswitch decisionAny {\n415: \tcase decisionCancel: // handle in code following this switch\n416: \tcase decisionExecute:\n417: \t\tklog.V(5).Infof(\"QS(%s): Dispatching request %#+v %#+v from its queue\", qs.qCfg.Name, req.descr1, req.descr2)\n418: \t\treturn true, false\n419: \tdefault:\n420: \t\t// This can not happen, all possible values are handled above\n421: \t\tklog.Errorf(\"QS(%s): Impossible decision (type %T, value %#+v) for request %#+v %#+v!  Treating as cancel\", qs.qCfg.Name, decisionAny, decisionAny, req.descr1, req.descr2)\n422: \t}\n423: \t// TODO(aaron-prindle) add metrics for this case\n424: \tklog.V(5).Infof(\"QS(%s): Ejecting request %#+v %#+v from its queue\", qs.qCfg.Name, req.descr1, req.descr2)\n425: \t// remove the request from the queue as its queue wait time has exceeded\n426: \tqueue := req.queue\n427: \tif req.removeFromQueueLocked() != nil {\n428: \t\tdefer qs.boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)\n429: \t\tqs.totRequestsWaiting--\n430: \t\tqs.totSeatsWaiting -= req.MaxSeats()\n431: \t\tqs.totRequestsRejected++\n432: \t\tqs.totRequestsCancelled++\n433: \t\tmetrics.AddReject(req.ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, req.fsName, \"time-out\")\n434: \t\tmetrics.AddRequestsInQueues(req.ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, req.fsName, -1)\n435: \t\tmetrics.AddSeatsInQueues(req.ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, req.fsName, -req.MaxSeats())\n436: \t\treq.NoteQueued(false)\n437: \t\tqs.reqsGaugePair.RequestsWaiting.Add(-1)\n438: \t\tqs.seatDemandIntegrator.Set(float64(qs.totSeatsInUse + qs.totSeatsWaiting))\n439: \t}\n440: \treturn false, qs.isIdleLocked()\n441: }\n442: \n443: func (qs *queueSet) IsIdle() bool {\n444: \tqs.lock.Lock()\n445: \tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n446: \treturn qs.isIdleLocked()\n447: }\n448: \n449: func (qs *queueSet) isIdleLocked() bool {\n450: \treturn qs.totRequestsWaiting == 0 && qs.totRequestsExecuting == 0\n451: }\n452: \n453: // lockAndSyncTime acquires the lock and updates the virtual time.\n454: // Doing them together avoids the mistake of modifying some queue state\n455: // before calling syncTimeLocked.\n456: func (qs *queueSet) lockAndSyncTime(ctx context.Context) {\n457: \tqs.lock.Lock()\n458: \tqs.syncTimeLocked(ctx)\n459: }\n460: \n461: // syncTimeLocked updates the virtual time based on the assumption\n462: // that the current state of the queues has been in effect since\n463: // `qs.lastRealTime`.  Thus, it should be invoked after acquiring the\n464: // lock and before modifying the state of any queue.\n465: func (qs *queueSet) syncTimeLocked(ctx context.Context) {\n466: \trealNow := qs.clock.Now()\n467: \ttimeSinceLast := realNow.Sub(qs.lastRealTime)\n468: \tqs.lastRealTime = realNow\n469: \tprevR := qs.currentR\n470: \tincrR := fqrequest.SeatsTimesDuration(qs.getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\n471: \tqs.currentR = prevR + incrR\n472: \tswitch {\n473: \tcase prevR > qs.currentR:\n474: \t\tklog.ErrorS(errors.New(\"queueset::currentR overflow\"), \"Overflow\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"when\", realNow.Format(nsTimeFmt), \"prevR\", prevR, \"incrR\", incrR, \"currentR\", qs.currentR)\n475: \tcase qs.currentR >= highR:\n476: \t\tqs.advanceEpoch(ctx, realNow, incrR)\n477: \t}\n478: \tmetrics.SetCurrentR(qs.qCfg.Name, qs.currentR.ToFloat())\n479: }\n480: \n481: // rDecrement is the amount by which the progress meter R is wound backwards\n482: // when needed to avoid overflow.\n483: const rDecrement = fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds / 2\n484: \n485: // highR is the threshold that triggers advance of the epoch.\n486: // That is, decrementing the global progress meter R by rDecrement.\n487: const highR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2\n488: \n489: // advanceEpoch subtracts rDecrement from the global progress meter R\n490: // and all the readings that have been taked from that meter.\n491: // The now and incrR parameters are only used to add info to the log messages.\n492: func (qs *queueSet) advanceEpoch(ctx context.Context, now time.Time, incrR fqrequest.SeatSeconds) {\n493: \toldR := qs.currentR\n494: \tqs.currentR -= rDecrement\n495: \tklog.InfoS(\"Advancing epoch\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"when\", now.Format(nsTimeFmt), \"oldR\", oldR, \"newR\", qs.currentR, \"incrR\", incrR)\n496: \tsuccess := true\n497: \tfor qIdx, queue := range qs.queues {\n498: \t\tif queue.requestsWaiting.Length() == 0 && queue.requestsExecuting.Len() == 0 {\n499: \t\t\t// Do not just decrement, the value could be quite outdated.\n500: \t\t\t// It is safe to reset to zero in this case, because the next request\n501: \t\t\t// will overwrite the zero with `qs.currentR`.\n502: \t\t\tqueue.nextDispatchR = 0\n503: \t\t\tcontinue\n504: \t\t}\n505: \t\toldNextDispatchR := queue.nextDispatchR\n506: \t\tqueue.nextDispatchR -= rDecrement\n507: \t\tif queue.nextDispatchR > oldNextDispatchR {\n508: \t\t\tklog.ErrorS(errors.New(\"queue::nextDispatchR underflow\"), \"Underflow\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"queue\", qIdx, \"oldNextDispatchR\", oldNextDispatchR, \"newNextDispatchR\", queue.nextDispatchR, \"incrR\", incrR)\n509: \t\t\tsuccess = false\n510: \t\t}\n511: \t\tqueue.requestsWaiting.Walk(func(req *request) bool {\n512: \t\t\toldArrivalR := req.arrivalR\n513: \t\t\treq.arrivalR -= rDecrement\n514: \t\t\tif req.arrivalR > oldArrivalR {\n515: \t\t\t\tklog.ErrorS(errors.New(\"request::arrivalR underflow\"), \"Underflow\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"queue\", qIdx, \"request\", *req, \"oldArrivalR\", oldArrivalR, \"incrR\", incrR)\n516: \t\t\t\tsuccess = false\n517: \t\t\t}\n518: \t\t\treturn true\n519: \t\t})\n520: \t}\n521: \tmetrics.AddEpochAdvance(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, success)\n522: }\n523: \n524: // getVirtualTimeRatio calculates the rate at which virtual time has\n525: // been advancing, according to the logic in `doc.go`.\n526: func (qs *queueSet) getVirtualTimeRatioLocked() float64 {\n527: \tactiveQueues := 0\n528: \tseatsRequested := 0\n529: \tfor _, queue := range qs.queues {\n530: \t\t// here we want the sum of the maximum width of the requests in this queue since our\n531: \t\t// goal is to find the maximum rate at which the queue could work.\n532: \t\tseatsRequested += (queue.seatsInUse + queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().MaxSeatsSum)\n533: \t\tif queue.requestsWaiting.Length() > 0 || queue.requestsExecuting.Len() > 0 {\n534: \t\t\tactiveQueues++\n535: \t\t}\n536: \t}\n537: \tif activeQueues == 0 {\n538: \t\treturn 0\n539: \t}\n540: \treturn math.Min(float64(seatsRequested), float64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)) / float64(activeQueues)\n541: }\n542: \n543: // shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked encapsulates the logic required\n544: // to validate and enqueue a request for the queueSet/QueueSet:\n545: // 1) Start with shuffle sharding, to pick a queue.\n546: // 2) Reject current request if there is not enough concurrency shares and\n547: // we are at max queue length\n548: // 3) If not rejected, create a request and enqueue\n549: // returns the enqueud request on a successful enqueue\n550: // returns nil in the case that there is no available concurrency or\n551: // the queuelengthlimit has been reached\n552: func (qs *queueSet) shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked(ctx context.Context, workEstimate *fqrequest.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}, queueNoteFn fq.QueueNoteFn) *request {\n553: \t// Start with the shuffle sharding, to pick a queue.\n554: \tqueueIdx := qs.shuffleShardLocked(hashValue, descr1, descr2)\n555: \tqueue := qs.queues[queueIdx]\n556: \n557: \tdefer qs.boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)\n558: \n559: \t// Create a request and enqueue\n560: \treq := &request{\n561: \t\tqs:                qs,\n562: \t\tfsName:            fsName,\n563: \t\tflowDistinguisher: flowDistinguisher,\n564: \t\tctx:               ctx,\n565: \t\tdecision:          qs.promiseFactory(nil, ctx, decisionCancel),\n566: \t\tarrivalTime:       qs.clock.Now(),\n567: \t\tarrivalR:          qs.currentR,\n568: \t\tqueue:             queue,\n569: \t\tdescr1:            descr1,\n570: \t\tdescr2:            descr2,\n571: \t\tqueueNoteFn:       queueNoteFn,\n572: \t\tworkEstimate:      qs.completeWorkEstimate(workEstimate),\n573: \t}\n574: \tif ok := qs.rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked(req); !ok {\n575: \t\treturn nil\n576: \t}\n577: \tmetrics.ObserveQueueLength(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, queue.requestsWaiting.Length())\n578: \treturn req\n579: }\n580: \n581: // shuffleShardLocked uses shuffle sharding to select a queue index\n582: // using the given hashValue and the shuffle sharding parameters of the queueSet.\n583: func (qs *queueSet) shuffleShardLocked(hashValue uint64, descr1, descr2 interface{}) int {\n584: \tvar backHand [8]int\n585: \t// Deal into a data structure, so that the order of visit below is not necessarily the order of the deal.\n586: \t// This removes bias in the case of flows with overlapping hands.\n587: \thand := qs.dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:])\n588: \thandSize := len(hand)\n589: \toffset := qs.enqueues % handSize\n590: \tqs.enqueues++\n591: \tbestQueueIdx := -1\n592: \tminQueueSeatSeconds := fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds\n593: \tfor i := 0; i < handSize; i++ {\n594: \t\tqueueIdx := hand[(offset+i)%handSize]\n595: \t\tqueue := qs.queues[queueIdx]\n596: \t\tqueueSum := queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum()\n597: \n598: \t\t// this is the total amount of work in seat-seconds for requests\n599: \t\t// waiting in this queue, we will select the queue with the minimum.\n600: \t\tthisQueueSeatSeconds := queueSum.TotalWorkSum\n601: \t\tklog.V(7).Infof(\"QS(%s): For request %#+v %#+v considering queue %d with sum: %#v and %d seats in use, nextDispatchR=%v\", qs.qCfg.Name, descr1, descr2, queueIdx, queueSum, queue.seatsInUse, queue.nextDispatchR)\n602: \t\tif thisQueueSeatSeconds < minQueueSeatSeconds {\n603: \t\t\tminQueueSeatSeconds = thisQueueSeatSeconds\n604: \t\t\tbestQueueIdx = queueIdx\n605: \t\t}\n606: \t}\n607: \tif klogV := klog.V(6); klogV.Enabled() {\n608: \t\tchosenQueue := qs.queues[bestQueueIdx]\n609: \t\tklogV.Infof(\"QS(%s) at t=%s R=%v: For request %#+v %#+v chose queue %d, with sum: %#v & %d seats in use & nextDispatchR=%v\", qs.qCfg.Name, qs.clock.Now().Format(nsTimeFmt), qs.currentR, descr1, descr2, bestQueueIdx, chosenQueue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum(), chosenQueue.seatsInUse, chosenQueue.nextDispatchR)\n610: \t}\n611: \treturn bestQueueIdx\n612: }\n613: \n614: // rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked rejects or enqueues the newly arrived\n615: // request, which has been assigned to a queue.  If up against the\n616: // queue length limit and the concurrency limit then returns false.\n617: // Otherwise enqueues and returns true.\n618: func (qs *queueSet) rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked(request *request) bool {\n619: \tqueue := request.queue\n620: \tcurQueueLength := queue.requestsWaiting.Length()\n621: \t// rejects the newly arrived request if resource criteria not met\n622: \tif qs.totSeatsInUse >= qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit &&\n623: \t\tcurQueueLength >= qs.qCfg.QueueLengthLimit {\n624: \t\treturn false\n625: \t}\n626: \n627: \tqs.enqueueToBoundLocked(request)\n628: \treturn true\n629: }\n630: \n631: // enqueues a request into its queue.\n632: func (qs *queueSet) enqueueToBoundLocked(request *request) {\n633: \tqueue := request.queue\n634: \tnow := qs.clock.Now()\n635: \tif queue.requestsWaiting.Length() == 0 && queue.requestsExecuting.Len() == 0 {\n636: \t\t// the queue\u2019s start R is set to the virtual time.\n637: \t\tqueue.nextDispatchR = qs.currentR\n638: \t\tklogV := klog.V(6)\n639: \t\tif klogV.Enabled() {\n640: \t\t\tklogV.Infof(\"QS(%s) at t=%s R=%v: initialized queue %d start R due to request %#+v %#+v\", qs.qCfg.Name, now.Format(nsTimeFmt), \tqs.seatDemandIntegrator.Set(float64(qs.totSeatsInUse + qs.totSeatsWaiting))\n651: }\n652: \n653: // dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked does as many dispatches as possible now.\n654: func (qs *queueSet) dispatchSansQueueLocked(ctx context.Context, workEstimate *fqrequest.WorkEstimate, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}) *request {\n660: \t// does not call \t\t\trequest.workEstimate, queue.index, queue.nextDispatchR)\n740: \t}\n741: \tqueue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()\n742: \treturn true\n743: }\n744: \n745: // canAccommodateSeatsLocked returns canAccommodateSeatsLocked(seats int) bool {\n749: \tswitch {\n750: \tcase qs.qCfg.DesiredNumQueues < 0:\n751: \t\t// This is code for exemption from limitation\n752: \t\treturn true\n753: \tcase seats A queue that can not use all those seats and does\n948: // not go empty accumulates a progresively earlier `virtualStart` compared\n949: // to queues that are using more than they are allocated.\n950: // The following hack addresses the first side of that inequity,\n951: // by insisting that dispatch in the virtual world not precede arrival.\n952: func (qs *queueSet) boundNextDispatchLocked(queue *queue) {\n953: \toldestReqFromMinQueue, _ := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n954: \tif oldestReqFromMinQueue == nil {\n955: \t\treturn\n956: \t}\n957: \tvar virtualStartBound = oldestReqFromMinQueue.arrivalR\n958: \tif queue.nextDispatchR < virtualStartBound {\n959: \t\tif klogV := klog.V(4); The integrals start when the\n31: // Integrator is created, and ends at the latest operation on the\n32: // Integrator.\n33: type Integrator interface {\n34: \tfcmetrics.Gauge\n35: \n36: \tGetResults() IntegratorResults\n37: \n38: \t// Return the results of integrating to now, and reset integration to start now\n39: \tReset() IntegratorResults\n40: }\n41: \n42: // IntegratorResults holds statistical abstracts of the integration\n43: type IntegratorResults struct {\n44: \tDuration  float64 //seconds\n45: \tAverage   float64 //time-weighted\n46: \tDeviation float64 //standard deviation: sqrt(avg((value-avg)^2))\n47: \tMin, Max  float64\n48: }\n49: \n50: // Equal tests for semantic equality.\n51: // This considers all NaN values to be equal to each other.\n52: func (x *IntegratorResults) Equal(y *IntegratorResults) bool {\n53: \treturn x == y || x != nil && y != nil && x.Duration == y.Duration && x.Min == y.Min && x.Max == y.Max && (x.Average == y.Average || math.IsNaN(x.Average) && math.IsNaN(y.Average)) && (x.Deviation == y.Deviation || math.IsNaN(x.Deviation) && math.IsNaN(y.Deviation))\n54: }\n55: \n56: type integrator struct {\n57: \tname one that uses the given clock and name\n67: func NewNamedIntegrator(clock clock.PassiveClock, name string) Integrator {\n68: \treturn &integrator{\n69: \t\tname:     name,\n70: \t\tclock:    clock,\n71: \t\tlastTime: clock.Now(),\n72: \t}\n73: }\n74: \n75: func (igr *integrator) Set(x float64) {\n76: \tigr.Lock()\n77: \tigr.setLocked(x)\n78: \tigr.Unlock()\n79: }\n80: \n81: func (igr *integrator) Add(deltaX float64) {\n82: \tigr.Lock()\n83: \tigr.setLocked(igr.x + deltaX)\n84: \tigr.Unlock()\n85: }\n86: \n87: func (igr *integrator) Inc() {\n88: \tigr.Add(1)\n89: }\n90: \n91: func (igr *integrator) Dec() {\n92: \tigr.Add(-1)\n93: }\n94: \n95: func (igr *integrator) SetToCurrentTime() {\n96: \tigr.Set(float64(time.Now().UnixNano()))\n97: }\n98: \n99: func (igr *integrator) setLocked(x float64) {\n100: \tigr.updateLocked()\n101: \tigr.x = x\n102: \tif x < igr.min {\n103: \t\tigr.min = x\n104: \t}\n105: \tif x > igr.max {\n106: \t\tigr.max = x\n107: \t}\n108: }\n109: \n110: func (igr *integrator) updateLocked() {\n111: \tnow := igr.clock.Now()\n112: \tdt := now.Sub(igr.lastTime).Seconds()\n113: \tigr.lastTime = now\n114: \tigr.moments = igr.moments.Add(ConstantMoments(dt, igr.x))\n115: }\n116: \n117: func (igr *integrator) GetResults() IntegratorResults {\n118: \tigr.Lock()\n119: \tdefer igr.Unlock()\n120: \treturn igr.getResultsLocked()\n121: }\n122: \n123: func (igr *integrator) Reset() IntegratorResults {\n124: \tigr.Lock()\n125: \tdefer igr.Unlock()\n126: \tresults := igr.getResultsLocked()\n127: \tigr.moments = Moments{}\n128: \tigr.min = igr.x\n129: \tigr.max = igr.x\n130: \treturn results\n131: }\n132: \n133: func (igr *integrator) getResultsLocked() (results IntegratorResults) {\n134: \tigr.updateLocked()\n135: \tresults.Min, results.Max = igr.min, igr.max\n136: \tresults.Duration = igr.moments.ElapsedSeconds\n137: \tresults.Average, results.Deviation = igr.moments.AvgAndStdDev()\n138: \treturn\n139: }\n140: \n141: // Moments are the integrals of the 0, 1, and 2 powers of some\n142: // variable X over some range of time.\n143: type Moments struct {\n144: \tElapsedSeconds float64 // integral of dt\n145: \tIntegralX      float64 // integral of x dt\n146: \tIntegralXX     float64 // integral of x*x dt\n147: }\n148: \n149: // ConstantMoments is for a constant X\n150: func ConstantMoments(dt, x float64) Moments {\n151: \treturn Moments{\n152: \t\tElapsedSeconds: dt,\n153: \t\tIntegralX:      x * dt,\n154: \t\tIntegralXX:     x * x * dt,\n155: \t}\n156: }\n157: \n158: // Add combines over two ranges of time\n159: func (igr Moments) Add(ogr Moments) Moments {\n160: \treturn Moments{\n161: \t\tElapsedSeconds: igr.ElapsedSeconds + ogr.ElapsedSeconds,\n162: \t\tIntegralX:      igr.IntegralX + ogr.IntegralX,\n163: \t\tIntegralXX:     igr.IntegralXX + ogr.IntegralXX,\n164: \t}\n165: }\n166: \n167: // Sub finds the difference between a range of time and a subrange\n168: func (igr Moments) Sub(ogr Moments) Moments {\n169: \treturn Moments{\n170: \t\tElapsedSeconds: igr.ElapsedSeconds - ogr.ElapsedSeconds,\n171: \t\tIntegralX:      igr.IntegralX - ogr.IntegralX,\n172: \t\tIntegralXX:     igr.IntegralXX - ogr.IntegralXX,\n173: \t}\n174: }\n175: \n176: // AvgAndStdDev returns the average and standard devation\n177: func (igr Moments) AvgAndStdDev() (float64, float64) {\n178: \tif igr.ElapsedSeconds <= 0 {\n179: \t\treturn math.NaN(), math.NaN()\n180: \t}\n181: \tavg := igr.IntegralX / igr.ElapsedSeconds\n182: \t// standard deviation is sqrt( average( (x - xbar)^2 ) )\n183: \t// = sqrt( Integral( x^2 + xbar^2 -2*x*xbar dt ) / Duration )\n184: \t// = sqrt( ( Integral( x^2 dt ) + Duration * xbar^2 - 2*xbar*Integral(x dt) ) / Duration)\n185: \t// = sqrt( Integral(x^2 dt)/Duration - xbar^2 )\n186: \tvariance := igr.IntegralXX/igr.ElapsedSeconds - avg*avg\n187: \tif variance >= 0 {\n188: \t\treturn avg, math.Sqrt(variance)\n189: \t}\n190: \treturn avg, math.NaN()\n191: }\n192: ",

// Interface defines how the API Priority and Fairness filter interacts with the underlying system.\\n45: type Interface interface {\\n46: \\t// Handle takes care of queuing and dispatching a request\\n47: \\t// characterized by the given digest. {
  "content": "# Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\nThe API Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet subsystem is the engine that enforces concurrency limits and inter-flow fairness for the Kubernetes apiserver. Its responsibilities are narrowly scoped: given a request already classified into a priority level, the QueueSet decides whether to execute it immediately, queue it until capacity becomes available, or reject it entirely.\n\n**What it is not responsible for:**\n\n- Classification of requests to priority levels or flow schemas \u2014 that belongs to `configController.startRequest()` in `apf_controller.go`.\n- The admission webhook pipeline, authentication, or authorization.\n- Scheduling of the work itself \u2014 it dispatches a signal; the actual handler runs in the caller's goroutine.\n\n**Upstream dependencies (inputs to the QueueSet):**\n\n- `configController` (`apf_controller.go`) supplies `QueuingConfig` (number of queues, queue depth, hand size) and `DispatchingConfig` (concurrency limit) through the two-phase construction API.\n- `WorkEstimate` (`request/width.go`) carries the work model: `InitialSeats`, `FinalSeats`, and `AdditionalLatency`.\n- `shufflesharding.Dealer` (`util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go`) provides the queue-selection algorithm.\n- `eventclock.Interface` (`fairqueuing/eventclock/`) is the monotonic time source used for virtual-time accounting.\n\n**Downstream dependencies (what the QueueSet hands off to):**\n\n- `apf_filter.go` receives the `fq.Request` object and calls `Finish(execFn)`, which blocks until the QueueSet dispatches or rejects the request.\n- `metrics` package (`flowcontrol/metrics/`) is updated at every state change: enqueue, dequeue, dispatch, reject, cancel.\n- `promise.WriteOnce` (`fairqueuing/promise/`) bridges the locking boundary between the dispatch path (which holds the QueueSet lock) and the blocking wait in the caller's goroutine (which must not hold the lock).\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 `QueueSetFactory` / `queueSetFactory`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:42`\n\nA factory that owns the clock and the `promiseFactoryFactory`. `BeginConstruction` validates the `QueuingConfig`, creates a `shufflesharding.Dealer` if queues are desired, and returns a `queueSetCompleter`. Construction is split into two phases so that configuration validation errors can be caught before committing to a concurrency allotment.\n\n### 2.2 `queueSet`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:85`\n\nThe core struct. It holds:\n\n- `queues []*queue` \u2014 the per-flow queues. The slice may be longer than `qCfg.DesiredNumQueues` while excess queues drain.\n- `currentR fqrequest.SeatSeconds` \u2014 the global virtual-time progress meter, the generalization of R from the FQSR paper.\n- `lastRealTime time.Time` \u2014 wall-clock time when R was last updated, used to advance R on each lock acquisition.\n- `robinIndex int` \u2014 the round-robin cursor for dispatch selection.\n- Aggregate counters: `totRequestsWaiting`, `totSeatsInUse`, `totSeatsWaiting`, etc.\n- `requestsExecutingSet sets.Set[*request]` \u2014 used only when `DesiredNumQueues < 1` (no-queue mode).\n\nA single `sync.Mutex` serializes all mutations. The naming convention `*Locked` means the caller must hold the lock; absence of that suffix means the method acquires and releases it.\n\n### 2.3 `queue`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:93`\n\nOne queue corresponds to one flow (a particular `flowDistinguisher` value within a priority level). Fields:\n\n- `requestsWaiting fifo` \u2014 FIFO of not-yet-dispatched requests.\n- `nextDispatchR fqrequest.SeatSeconds` \u2014 the virtual start time of the queue; increased by each dispatched request's total work, decreased by the actual-vs-estimated service time difference upon completion.\n- `requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]` \u2014 executing requests from this queue.\n- `seatsInUse int` \u2014 seat occupancy from this queue's executing requests.\n\n### 2.4 `request`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:33`\n\nA transient container wrapping one incoming HTTP request. Key fields:\n\n- `workEstimate completedWorkEstimate` \u2014 holds `InitialSeats`, `FinalSeats`, `AdditionalLatency`, and the derived `totalWork` (seat-seconds) used in virtual-time accounting.\n- `arrivalR fqrequest.SeatSeconds` \u2014 the value of `currentR` when the request arrived; used as the floor for `nextDispatchR` in the anti-windup hack.\n- `decision promise.WriteOnce` \u2014 set to `decisionExecute` or `decisionCancel`; the caller blocks on `decision.Get()` in `wait()`.\n- `removeFromQueueLocked removeFromFIFOFunc` \u2014 O(1) closure to remove this request from its FIFO.\n\n### 2.5 `fifo` / `requestFIFO`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go:42`\n\nA doubly-linked list (`container/list.List`) that maintains running sums (`queueSum`) of `InitialSeats`, `MaxSeats`, and `TotalWork` across all waiting requests. These sums are used by the shuffle-sharding queue selection (to pick the queue with the least pending work) and by the virtual-time ratio computation (to know total seat demand). Removal via `removeFromFIFOFunc` is O(1) by holding the `*list.Element`.\n\n### 2.6 `promise.WriteOnce`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/promise/promise.go`\n\nA write-once, multiple-reader synchronization primitive. `Set` stores a value and closes an internal channel (using `sync.Once`). `Get` blocks on either that channel or a context-done channel, whichever fires first \u2014 delivering `doneVal` if the context expires. This lets the dispatch path (lock held, goroutine is the worker) communicate a decision to the caller's goroutine (no lock, potentially blocked) without holding the lock across a channel send.\n\n### 2.7 `shufflesharding.Dealer`\n\n**File:** `util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go:40`\n\nImplements the shuffle-sharding algorithm used for queue selection. `Deal(hashValue, pick)` derives `handSize` card indices from a hash value using a sequence of modular divisions, avoiding allocation by computing index adjustments in-place. The Dealer is constructed with `deckSize` = number of queues and `handSize` from the API object. `RequiredEntropyBits` ensures the hash value provides sufficient randomness.\n\n### 2.8 `WorkEstimate` and `SeatSeconds`\n\n**Files:** `request/width.go:34`, `request/seat_seconds.go`\n\n`WorkEstimate` is the caller-supplied work model. The QueueSet converts it to a `completedWorkEstimate` with two derived quantities:\n\n```\ninitialWork = InitialSeats \u00d7 estimatedServiceDuration   (\u22483ms fixed constant)\nfinalWork   = FinalSeats   \u00d7 AdditionalLatency\ntotalWork   = initialWork + finalWork\n```\n\n`SeatSeconds` is a fixed-point `uint64` with 10^8 scale. This scale was chosen to represent both nanosecond-precision durations and many-seat requests without overflow for practical lifetimes.\n\n### 2.9 `configController` and `priorityLevelState`\n\n**File:** `apf_controller.go:121`\n\nThe outer controller that owns the lifecycle of all QueueSets. `priorityLevelState` pairs a `PriorityLevelConfiguration` API object with its live `QueueSet`, plus borrowing statistics:\n\n- `nominalCL`, `minCL`, `maxCL` \u2014 the concurrency limits derived from config.\n- `currentCL` \u2014 the dynamically adjusted limit after borrowing.\n- `seatDemandIntegrator fq.Integrator` \u2014 time-weighted integral of `seatsInUse + seatsWaiting`, reset every borrowing adjustment period.\n- `seatDemandStats` \u2014 smoothed demand statistics feeding the borrowing algorithm.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control and Request Flow\n\nThe flow has four logical steps:\n\n### Step 0: Classification (outside QueueSet)\n\n`configController.startRequest()` (`apf_controller.go:1022`) holds a read lock and walks `cfgCtlr.flowSchemas` in precedence order. The first `FlowSchema` whose rules match the `RequestDigest` (user + `RequestInfo`) is selected. From the matched schema:\n\n1. `plName` identifies the `priorityLevelState`.\n2. `computeFlowDistinguisher()` extracts a string (user name or namespace) per the schema's `DistinguisherMethod`.\n3. `hashFlowID(fsName, flowDistinguisher)` computes a SHA-256-based `uint64` hash to seed the shuffle shard.\n4. `workEstimator()` is called to obtain the `WorkEstimate` \u2014 different estimators apply for list, mutating, and watch requests.\n5. `plState.queues.StartRequest(ctx, &workEstimate, hashValue, ...)` is called.\n\nExempt priority levels (`DesiredNumQueues < 0`) bypass all queuing and concurrency checks.\n\n### Step 1: Queue Assignment and Admission (`StartRequest`)\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:308`\n\n```\nStartRequest:\n  lockAndSyncTime(ctx)         \u2190 acquire lock, advance currentR\n  if DesiredNumQueues < 1:\n    if !canAccommodateSeats: reject\n    else: dispatchSansQueueLocked \u2192 return immediately-executing request\n  else:\n    shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked\n    dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked\n    return queued request\n```\n\n**`lockAndSyncTime` / `syncTimeLocked`** (`queueset.go:456`): Every time the lock is acquired, the virtual clock advances:\n\n```\ntimeSinceLast = now - lastRealTime\nincrR = getVirtualTimeRatioLocked() \u00d7 timeSinceLast\ncurrentR += incrR\n```\n\n`getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()` (`queueset.go:526`) returns:\n\n```\nmin(totalSeatsRequested, ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n```\n\nwhere `totalSeatsRequested` is the sum over all queues of `seatsInUse + MaxSeatsSum(waiting)`. This is the FQSR generalization of the Weighted Fair Queuing virtual-time increment: each active queue is allocated an equal share of the minimum of actual demand and capacity.\n\n**`shuffleShardLocked`** (`queueset.go:583`): Calls `dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:])` to get `handSize` candidate queue indices, then iterates them in a round-robin-offset order (using `enqueues % handSize` as starting offset to avoid bias with overlapping hands) and picks the queue with the minimum `TotalWorkSum` (pending seat-seconds). This selection minimizes head-of-line blocking for the incoming flow while distributing different flows across different queues.\n\n**`rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked`** (`queueset.go:618`): Rejects if both `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit` AND `curQueueLength >= QueueLengthLimit`. Otherwise calls `enqueueToBoundLocked`. If the queue was empty, `nextDispatchR` is reset to `currentR` so it does not inherit a stale position. The request's `arrivalR` records `currentR` at this moment.\n\n### Step 2: Dispatch Loop (`dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked`)\n\n**File:** `queueset.go:654`\n\n```go\nfor totRequestsWaiting != 0 &&\n    totSeatsInUse < ConcurrencyLimit &&\n    dispatchLocked() {}\n```\n\n**`findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`** (`queueset.go:776`): Scans all queues in round-robin order (updating `robinIndex` to avoid starvation). For each queue with a waiting request, it computes:\n\n```\nvirtualFinish = queue.nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()\n```\n\nThe queue with the minimum `virtualFinish` is selected \u2014 this is the FQSR dispatch criterion. After selection, if `oldestRequest.MaxSeats() > ConcurrencyLimit`, dispatch is blocked (single-request oversubscription case). Otherwise the request is removed from the FIFO.\n\n**On dispatch** (`queueset.go:695`):\n\n1. `request.decision.Set(decisionExecute)` wakes the blocked caller.\n2. `queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()` advances the queue's virtual clock by the cost of this request.\n3. `totSeatsInUse += request.MaxSeats()`, `queue.seatsInUse += MaxSeats`.\n4. `boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)` is deferred to apply the anti-windup bound.\n\n### Step 3: Caller Blocks in `wait()` / `Finish()`\n\n**File:** `queueset.go:397`\n\nThe `Finish(execFn)` call in `apf_filter.go:179` proceeds as:\n\n```\nexec, idle = req.wait()    \u2190 blocks on promise\nif exec: execFn(); finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible\n```\n\n`wait()` blocks on `req.decision.Get()`, which in turn blocks on either:\n- The `setCh` channel (closed by `dispatchLocked` or `dispatchSansQueueLocked`), or\n- `ctx.Done()` \u2014 context cancellation, in which case `doneVal = decisionCancel` is injected.\n\nIf cancelled while queued, `wait()` re-acquires the lock and removes the request from its FIFO via `removeFromQueueLocked`, adjusting all counters and metrics.\n\n### Step 4: Request Completion (`finishRequestLocked`)\n\n**File:** `queueset.go:863`\n\nWhen the handler returns, `finishRequestLocked` is called with the lock held:\n\n1. Decrements `totRequestsExecuting` and global seat/request metrics.\n2. If `AdditionalLatency > 0`, defers seat release with `clock.EventAfterDuration` \u2014 a goroutine fires after the latency, re-acquires the lock, calls `releaseSeatsLocked`, and runs `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked`. The actual HTTP response has already been sent; this linger models the work done by watch fan-out, etc.\n3. If `AdditionalLatency == 0`, seats are released immediately.\n4. `queue.nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(InitialSeats, estimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration)`: the queue's virtual start is adjusted by the difference between estimated and actual service time. If a request finishes faster than estimated, the queue is credited backward; if slower, the adjustment is positive (still bounded by the anti-windup hack).\n5. `boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)`: clamps `nextDispatchR` to be no earlier than the oldest waiting request's `arrivalR`.\n6. `removeQueueIfEmptyLocked`: if `len(queues) > DesiredNumQueues` and this queue is empty, it is spliced out and all subsequent indices are decremented.\n7. `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` runs again, potentially unblocking requests that were seat-limited.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Overflow Mitigation: Epoch Advancement\n\n`currentR` is a `uint64` fixed-point number. Over a long-running apiserver it would overflow. When `currentR >= highR` (approximately 75% of `MaxSeatSeconds`), `advanceEpoch` (`queueset.go:492`) subtracts `rDecrement = MaxSeatSeconds/2` from `currentR` and from every queue's `nextDispatchR` and every waiting request's `arrivalR`. Underflow during subtraction is logged as an error but does not crash; the system continues operating with potentially degraded fairness.\n\n### 4.2 Queue Rejection Policy\n\nRejection at `StartRequest` occurs when:\n\n- **No-queue mode** (`DesiredNumQueues < 1`): `totSeatsInUse + MaxSeats > ConcurrencyLimit`.\n- **Queue mode**: both `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit` AND `curQueueLength >= QueueLengthLimit`. This is a logical-AND condition: if even one slot is free in the queue, the request is held rather than rejected. The intent is to absorb short-duration bursts.\n\n### 4.3 Work Estimation Approximations\n\n`estimatedServiceDuration` is hardcoded to `3ms` (`queueset.go:215`). This is used only for the `initialWork` term of `totalWork` and for `boundNextDispatchLocked`. If real request durations deviate significantly from 3 ms, the virtual-time advance per request is wrong, which degrades fairness but does not violate the concurrency limit. The `FinalSeats \u00d7 AdditionalLatency` term uses actual measured latency from the work estimator, so watch requests (which linger with high seat counts) are modeled accurately.\n\n### 4.4 Anti-Windup Bound Tradeoff\n\nThe `boundNextDispatchLocked` hack (`queueset.go:952`) prevents a queue that ran with fewer seats than its fair share from accumulating an arbitrarily advanced virtual clock, which would let it cut ahead of all other queues. The bound guarantees `nextDispatchR >= arrivalR` of the oldest waiting request. This breaks the strict FQSR guarantee of work conservation in exchange for preventing starvation; a queue cannot get \"credit\" beyond what it actually used.\n\n### 4.5 Seat-Request Oversubscription\n\nWhen the head-of-queue request requires more seats than the total `ConcurrencyLimit`, `canAccommodateSeatsLocked` (`queueset.go:748`) blocks dispatch unless the queueset is completely empty (`totRequestsExecuting == 0`). This prevents deadlock (the oversize request would never dispatch if any other request were running), but it can cause the queueset to stall if requests ahead of it are slow to finish.\n\n### 4.6 Configuration Change Without Disruption\n\nQueue count reduction uses attrition: queues are only removed when they drain naturally (`removeQueueIfEmptyLocked`). Queue count increase is immediate (`setConfiguration` appends new queues). This means a reduction takes time proportional to the slowest current request, and in the interim the old queues continue to be considered for dispatch, slightly diluting the new configuration.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Risks\n\n### 5.1 `QueueSetFactory` / `promiseFactoryFactory`\n\nThe public factory is `NewQueueSetFactory(c eventclock.Interface)` (`queueset.go:170`). Tests can substitute `newTestableQueueSetFactory` with a custom `promiseFactoryFactory`. The `promiseFactory` type is `func(initial interface{}, doneCtx context.Context, doneVal interface{}) promise.WriteOnce`. This is the only hook that changes locking semantics \u2014 a wrong implementation here can deadlock (if `Set` blocks while the lock is held) or cause data races (if `Get` is called under the lock).\n\n### 5.2 `WorkEstimatorFunc`\n\n**File:** `request/width.go:89`\n\nThe work estimator is pluggable via `WorkEstimatorFunc`. Three estimators are composed: list (object-count based), mutating (watch-count based), and a default (1 seat). Operators can influence behavior by adjusting `WorkEstimatorConfig` fields such as `MinimumSeats`, `MaximumListSeatsLimit`, and `MaximumMutatingSeatsLimit`. Misconfiguring these can cause either underestimation (allowing too many heavy requests through) or overestimation (starving legitimate traffic).\n\n### 5.3 Borrowing Adjustment via `updateBorrowing`\n\n**File:** `apf_controller.go:393`\n\nThe borrowing loop runs every `borrowingAdjustmentPeriod` (10 seconds) and calls `computeConcurrencyAllocation` to solve a bounded allocation problem. Each priority level has `[minCL, maxCL]` bounds and a `target` derived from smoothed demand. The smoothing coefficient `seatDemandSmoothingCoefficient = 0.977` gives a half-life of approximately 5 minutes. Operators can indirectly tune this by adjusting `lendablePercent` and `borrowingLimitPercent` in `PriorityLevelConfiguration`. Setting `lendablePercent = 0` makes a level non-lendable (it always holds its nominal allocation); setting `borrowingLimitPercent = nil` allows unlimited borrowing up to `serverConcurrencyLimit`.\n\nRisk: the borrowing algorithm converges every 10 seconds. A sustained burst that lasts under 10 seconds and then subsides does not trigger reborrowing back, because `seatDemandStats.smoothed` decays slowly. In practice this means transiently busy levels hold borrowed capacity for minutes after the burst ends.\n\n### 5.4 `QueueNoteFn`\n\n`StartRequest` accepts a `QueueNoteFn fq.QueueNoteFn` callback that is invoked with `true` when the request enters a queue and `false` when it leaves (either dispatched or rejected). This is used by `apf_filter.go` to track `startWaitingTime` for queue wait latency metrics and for `httplog.AddKeyValue`.\n\n### 5.5 Mandatory FlowSchemas and Priority Levels\n\n`configController` ensures the `exempt` and `catch-all` FlowSchemas and PriorityLevelConfigurations always exist, creating imagined stand-ins with `imaginePL` if the API objects are missing. The catch-all priority level uses `DesiredNumQueues > 0` by the default mandatory config, so unauthenticated or misclassified traffic is queued rather than rejected outright \u2014 a safety mechanism that also means the catch-all level can become a congestion point.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance\n\nThe `sync.Mutex` in `queueSet` serializes all state changes, including `StartRequest`, `Finish`, and every `EventAfterDuration` callback for lingering seats. At high request rates this mutex can become a bottleneck. Each priority level has its own QueueSet with its own lock, so the contention is scoped to a single priority level.\n\nThe `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` loop runs `O(queues)` iterations per request arrival and per request completion. With 128 queues (the default `WorkloadDefault` configuration) this is 128 iterations for each event. At 1000 requests/second per priority level and 128 queues, the dispatch loop runs ~128,000 iterations/second \u2014 negligible CPU, but it does hold the lock throughout.\n\nThe `syncTimeLocked` call at every lock acquisition computes `getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()` which itself iterates over all queues to sum seat demand. This is another `O(queues)` scan per lock acquisition.\n\n### 6.2 Reliability\n\nThe `promise.WriteOnce` design ensures that `Finish()` never returns while `execFn()` is still running, even if the context is cancelled. This is guaranteed by the deferred structure in `Finish` (`queueset.go:386`): cancellation can only be observed after `wait()` returns, and if `wait()` returned `exec=true` then `execFn` runs to completion before `finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible` is called.\n\nLingering seat release via `EventAfterDuration` spawns a goroutine per request with `FinalSeats > 0`. If the API server is under heavy load with many watch completions, these goroutines pile up. Each one re-acquires the QueueSet lock, so they serialize correctly, but the goroutine creation is not bounded beyond the total executing request count.\n\n### 6.3 Maintainability\n\nThe two-level locking structure (outer `configController.lock sync.RWMutex` and inner per-QueueSet `sync.Mutex`) is documented but requires care: `startRequest` holds a read lock on the controller while calling into the QueueSet, which holds its own lock. The `Handle \u2192 startRequest \u2192 QueueSet.StartRequest` call chain spans both locks. Extending this with additional blocking inside `StartRequest` (e.g., a third data structure lock) risks deadlock.\n\nThe virtual time epoch advancement (`advanceEpoch`) mutates every queue and every waiting request's `arrivalR`. This O(requests \u00d7 queues) operation runs while the lock is held. In a pathological scenario with thousands of queued requests, this could stall dispatch for a measurable period.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Critical Files and Directories\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go` | Public interface: `QueueSetFactory`, `QueueSet`, `Request`, `QueuingConfig`, `DispatchingConfig` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go` | Core FQSR implementation: virtual time, dispatch loop, enqueue, finish |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go` | Data structures: `request`, `queue`, `completedWorkEstimate`, `queueSum` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go` | FIFO with O(1) remove and running `queueSum` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/promise/promise.go` | Write-once coordination primitive for dispatch decisions |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go` | Config controller: lifecycle, FlowSchema matching, borrowing adjustment |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_filter.go` | Entry point: `Interface.Handle()`, `New()`, `NewTestable()` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/conc_alloc.go` | Bounded concurrency allocation algorithm for borrowing |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/integrator.go` | Time-weighted integrator for seat demand statistics |\n| `Dealer`: entropy-efficient Fisher-Yates card-deal for queue selection |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/eventclock/` | Clock abstraction for testable time-advance |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/metrics/` | Prometheus metrics surface: queued seats, executing seats, dispatch timing |\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/documentation.md"
