{
  "content": "# Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\nThe API Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet subsystem is the engine that enforces concurrency limits and inter-flow fairness for the Kubernetes apiserver. Its responsibilities are narrowly scoped: given a request already classified into a priority level, the QueueSet decides whether to execute it immediately, queue it until capacity becomes available, or reject it entirely.\n\n**What it is not responsible for:**\n\n- Classification of requests to priority levels or flow schemas \u2014 that belongs to `configController.startRequest()` in `apf_controller.go`.\n- The admission webhook pipeline, authentication, or authorization.\n- Scheduling of the work itself \u2014 it dispatches a signal; the actual handler runs in the caller's goroutine.\n\n**Upstream dependencies (inputs to the QueueSet):**\n\n- `configController` (`apf_controller.go`) supplies `QueuingConfig` (number of queues, queue depth, hand size) and `DispatchingConfig` (concurrency limit) through the two-phase construction API.\n- `WorkEstimate` (`request/width.go`) carries the work model: `InitialSeats`, `FinalSeats`, and `AdditionalLatency`.\n- `shufflesharding.Dealer` (`util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go`) provides the queue-selection algorithm.\n- `eventclock.Interface` (`fairqueuing/eventclock/`) is the monotonic time source used for virtual-time accounting.\n\n**Downstream dependencies (what the QueueSet hands off to):**\n\n- `apf_filter.go` receives the `fq.Request` object and calls `Finish(execFn)`, which blocks until the QueueSet dispatches or rejects the request.\n- `metrics` package (`flowcontrol/metrics/`) is updated at every state change: enqueue, dequeue, dispatch, reject, cancel.\n- `promise.WriteOnce` (`fairqueuing/promise/`) bridges the locking boundary between the dispatch path (which holds the QueueSet lock) and the blocking wait in the caller's goroutine (which must not hold the lock).\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 `QueueSetFactory` / `queueSetFactory`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:42`\n\nA factory that owns the clock and the `promiseFactoryFactory`. `BeginConstruction` validates the `QueuingConfig`, creates a `shufflesharding.Dealer` if queues are desired, and returns a `queueSetCompleter`. Construction is split into two phases so that configuration validation errors can be caught before committing to a concurrency allotment.\n\n### 2.2 `queueSet`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:85`\n\nThe core struct. It holds:\n\n- `queues []*queue` \u2014 the per-flow queues. The slice may be longer than `qCfg.DesiredNumQueues` while excess queues drain.\n- `currentR fqrequest.SeatSeconds` \u2014 the global virtual-time progress meter, the generalization of R from the FQSR paper.\n- `lastRealTime time.Time` \u2014 wall-clock time when R was last updated, used to advance R on each lock acquisition.\n- `robinIndex int` \u2014 the round-robin cursor for dispatch selection.\n- Aggregate counters: `totRequestsWaiting`, `totSeatsInUse`, `totSeatsWaiting`, etc.\n- `requestsExecutingSet sets.Set[*request]` \u2014 used only when `DesiredNumQueues < 1` (no-queue mode).\n\nA single `sync.Mutex` serializes all mutations. The naming convention `*Locked` means the caller must hold the lock; absence of that suffix means the method acquires and releases it.\n\n### 2.3 `queue`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:93`\n\nOne queue corresponds to one flow (a particular `flowDistinguisher` value within a priority level). Fields:\n\n- `requestsWaiting fifo` \u2014 FIFO of not-yet-dispatched requests.\n- `nextDispatchR fqrequest.SeatSeconds` \u2014 the virtual start time of the queue; increased by each dispatched request's total work, decreased by the actual-vs-estimated service time difference upon completion.\n- `requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]` \u2014 executing requests from this queue.\n- `seatsInUse int` \u2014 seat occupancy from this queue's executing requests.\n\n### 2.4 `request`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:33`\n\nA transient container wrapping one incoming HTTP request. Key fields:\n\n- `workEstimate completedWorkEstimate` \u2014 holds `InitialSeats`, `FinalSeats`, `AdditionalLatency`, and the derived `totalWork` (seat-seconds) used in virtual-time accounting.\n- `arrivalR fqrequest.SeatSeconds` \u2014 the value of `currentR` when the request arrived; used as the floor for `nextDispatchR` in the anti-windup hack.\n- `decision promise.WriteOnce` \u2014 set to `decisionExecute` or `decisionCancel`; the caller blocks on `decision.Get()` in `wait()`.\n- `removeFromQueueLocked removeFromFIFOFunc` \u2014 O(1) closure to remove this request from its FIFO.\n\n### 2.5 `fifo` / `requestFIFO`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go:42`\n\nA doubly-linked list (`container/list.List`) that maintains running sums (`queueSum`) of `InitialSeats`, `MaxSeats`, and `TotalWork` across all waiting requests. These sums are used by the shuffle-sharding queue selection (to pick the queue with the least pending work) and by the virtual-time ratio computation (to know total seat demand). Removal via `removeFromFIFOFunc` is O(1) by holding the `*list.Element`.\n\n### 2.6 `promise.WriteOnce`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/promise/promise.go`\n\nA write-once, multiple-reader synchronization primitive. `Set` stores a value and closes an internal channel (using `sync.Once`). `Get` blocks on either that channel or a context-done channel, whichever fires first \u2014 delivering `doneVal` if the context expires. This lets the dispatch path (lock held, goroutine is the worker) communicate a decision to the caller's goroutine (no lock, potentially blocked) without holding the lock across a channel send.\n\n### 2.7 `shufflesharding.Dealer`\n\n**File:** `util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go:40`\n\nImplements the shuffle-sharding algorithm used for queue selection. `Deal(hashValue, pick)` derives `handSize` card indices from a hash value using a sequence of modular divisions, avoiding allocation by computing index adjustments in-place. The Dealer is constructed with `deckSize` = number of queues and `handSize` from the API object. `RequiredEntropyBits` ensures the hash value provides sufficient randomness.\n\n### 2.8 `WorkEstimate` and `SeatSeconds`\n\n**Files:** `request/width.go:34`, `request/seat_seconds.go`\n\n`WorkEstimate` is the caller-supplied work model. The QueueSet converts it to a `completedWorkEstimate` with two derived quantities:\n\n```\ninitialWork = InitialSeats \u00d7 estimatedServiceDuration   (\u22483ms fixed constant)\nfinalWork   = FinalSeats   \u00d7 AdditionalLatency\ntotalWork   = initialWork + finalWork\n```\n\n`SeatSeconds` is a fixed-point `uint64` with 10^8 scale. This scale was chosen to represent both nanosecond-precision durations and many-seat requests without overflow for practical lifetimes.\n\n### 2.9 `configController` and `priorityLevelState`\n\n**File:** `apf_controller.go:121`\n\nThe outer controller that owns the lifecycle of all QueueSets. `priorityLevelState` pairs a `PriorityLevelConfiguration` API object with its live `QueueSet`, plus borrowing statistics:\n\n- `nominalCL`, `minCL`, `maxCL` \u2014 the concurrency limits derived from config.\n- `currentCL` \u2014 the dynamically adjusted limit after borrowing.\n- `seatDemandIntegrator fq.Integrator` \u2014 time-weighted integral of `seatsInUse + seatsWaiting`, reset every borrowing adjustment period.\n- `seatDemandStats` \u2014 smoothed demand statistics feeding the borrowing algorithm.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control and Request Flow\n\nThe flow has four logical steps:\n\n### Step 0: Classification (outside QueueSet)\n\n`configController.startRequest()` (`apf_controller.go:1022`) holds a read lock and walks `cfgCtlr.flowSchemas` in precedence order. The first `FlowSchema` whose rules match the `RequestDigest` (user + `RequestInfo`) is selected. From the matched schema:\n\n1. `plName` identifies the `priorityLevelState`.\n2. `computeFlowDistinguisher()` extracts a string (user name or namespace) per the schema's `DistinguisherMethod`.\n3. `hashFlowID(fsName, flowDistinguisher)` computes a SHA-256-based `uint64` hash to seed the shuffle shard.\n4. `workEstimator()` is called to obtain the `WorkEstimate` \u2014 different estimators apply for list, mutating, and watch requests.\n5. `plState.queues.StartRequest(ctx, &workEstimate, hashValue, ...)` is called.\n\nExempt priority levels (`DesiredNumQueues < 0`) bypass all queuing and concurrency checks.\n\n### Step 1: Queue Assignment and Admission (`StartRequest`)\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:308`\n\n```\nStartRequest:\n  lockAndSyncTime(ctx)         \u2190 acquire lock, advance currentR\n  if DesiredNumQueues < 1:\n    if !canAccommodateSeats: reject\n    else: dispatchSansQueueLocked \u2192 return immediately-executing request\n  else:\n    shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked\n    dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked\n    return queued request\n```\n\n**`lockAndSyncTime` / `syncTimeLocked`** (`queueset.go:456`): Every time the lock is acquired, the virtual clock advances:\n\n```\ntimeSinceLast = now - lastRealTime\nincrR = getVirtualTimeRatioLocked() \u00d7 timeSinceLast\ncurrentR += incrR\n```\n\n`getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()` (`queueset.go:526`) returns:\n\n```\nmin(totalSeatsRequested, ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n```\n\nwhere `totalSeatsRequested` is the sum over all queues of `seatsInUse + MaxSeatsSum(waiting)`. This is the FQSR generalization of the Weighted Fair Queuing virtual-time increment: each active queue is allocated an equal share of the minimum of actual demand and capacity.\n\n**`shuffleShardLocked`** (`queueset.go:583`): Calls `dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:])` to get `handSize` candidate queue indices, then iterates them in a round-robin-offset order (using `enqueues % handSize` as starting offset to avoid bias with overlapping hands) and picks the queue with the minimum `TotalWorkSum` (pending seat-seconds). This selection minimizes head-of-line blocking for the incoming flow while distributing different flows across different queues.\n\n**`rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked`** (`queueset.go:618`): Rejects if both `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit` AND `curQueueLength >= QueueLengthLimit`. Otherwise calls `enqueueToBoundLocked`. If the queue was empty, `nextDispatchR` is reset to `currentR` so it does not inherit a stale position. The request's `arrivalR` records `currentR` at this moment.\n\n### Step 2: Dispatch Loop (`dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked`)\n\n**File:** `queueset.go:654`\n\n```go\nfor totRequestsWaiting != 0 &&\n    totSeatsInUse < ConcurrencyLimit &&\n    dispatchLocked() {}\n```\n\n**`findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`** (`queueset.go:776`): Scans all queues in round-robin order (updating `robinIndex` to avoid starvation). For each queue with a waiting request, it computes:\n\n```\nvirtualFinish = queue.nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()\n```\n\nThe queue with the minimum `virtualFinish` is selected \u2014 this is the FQSR dispatch criterion. After selection, if `oldestRequest.MaxSeats() > ConcurrencyLimit`, dispatch is blocked (single-request oversubscription case). Otherwise the request is removed from the FIFO.\n\n**On dispatch** (`queueset.go:695`):\n\n1. `request.decision.Set(decisionExecute)` wakes the blocked caller.\n2. `queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()` advances the queue's virtual clock by the cost of this request.\n3. `totSeatsInUse += request.MaxSeats()`, `queue.seatsInUse += MaxSeats`.\n4. `boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)` is deferred to apply the anti-windup bound.\n\n### Step 3: Caller Blocks in `wait()` / `Finish()`\n\n**File:** `queueset.go:397`\n\nThe `Finish(execFn)` call in `apf_filter.go:179` proceeds as:\n\n```\nexec, idle = req.wait()    \u2190 blocks on promise\nif exec: execFn(); finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible\n```\n\n`wait()` blocks on `req.decision.Get()`, which in turn blocks on either:\n- The `setCh` channel (closed by `dispatchLocked` or `dispatchSansQueueLocked`), or\n- `ctx.Done()` \u2014 context cancellation, in which case `doneVal = decisionCancel` is injected.\n\nIf cancelled while queued, `wait()` re-acquires the lock and removes the request from its FIFO via `removeFromQueueLocked`, adjusting all counters and metrics.\n\n### Step 4: Request Completion (`finishRequestLocked`)\n\n**File:** `queueset.go:863`\n\nWhen the handler returns, `finishRequestLocked` is called with the lock held:\n\n1. Decrements `totRequestsExecuting` and global seat/request metrics.\n2. If `AdditionalLatency > 0`, defers seat release with `clock.EventAfterDuration` \u2014 a goroutine fires after the latency, re-acquires the lock, calls `releaseSeatsLocked`, and runs `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked`. The actual HTTP response has already been sent; this linger models the work done by watch fan-out, etc.\n3. If `AdditionalLatency == 0`, seats are released immediately.\n4. `queue.nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(InitialSeats, estimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration)`: the queue's virtual start is adjusted by the difference between estimated and actual service time. If a request finishes faster than estimated, the queue is credited backward; if slower, the adjustment is positive (still bounded by the anti-windup hack).\n5. `boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)`: clamps `nextDispatchR` to be no earlier than the oldest waiting request's `arrivalR`.\n6. `removeQueueIfEmptyLocked`: if `len(queues) > DesiredNumQueues` and this queue is empty, it is spliced out and all subsequent indices are decremented.\n7. `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` runs again, potentially unblocking requests that were seat-limited.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Overflow Mitigation: Epoch Advancement\n\n`currentR` is a `uint64` fixed-point number. Over a long-running apiserver it would overflow. When `currentR >= highR` (approximately 75% of `MaxSeatSeconds`), `advanceEpoch` (`queueset.go:492`) subtracts `rDecrement = MaxSeatSeconds/2` from `currentR` and from every queue's `nextDispatchR` and every waiting request's `arrivalR`. Underflow during subtraction is logged as an error but does not crash; the system continues operating with potentially degraded fairness.\n\n### 4.2 Queue Rejection Policy\n\nRejection at `StartRequest` occurs when:\n\n- **No-queue mode** (`DesiredNumQueues < 1`): `totSeatsInUse + MaxSeats > ConcurrencyLimit`.\n- **Queue mode**: both `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit` AND `curQueueLength >= QueueLengthLimit`. This is a logical-AND condition: if even one slot is free in the queue, the request is held rather than rejected. The intent is to absorb short-duration bursts.\n\n### 4.3 Work Estimation Approximations\n\n`estimatedServiceDuration` is hardcoded to `3ms` (`queueset.go:215`). This is used only for the `initialWork` term of `totalWork` and for `boundNextDispatchLocked`. If real request durations deviate significantly from 3 ms, the virtual-time advance per request is wrong, which degrades fairness but does not violate the concurrency limit. The `FinalSeats \u00d7 AdditionalLatency` term uses actual measured latency from the work estimator, so watch requests (which linger with high seat counts) are modeled accurately.\n\n### 4.4 Anti-Windup Bound Tradeoff\n\nThe `boundNextDispatchLocked` hack (`queueset.go:952`) prevents a queue that ran with fewer seats than its fair share from accumulating an arbitrarily advanced virtual clock, which would let it cut ahead of all other queues. The bound guarantees `nextDispatchR >= arrivalR` of the oldest waiting request. This breaks the strict FQSR guarantee of work conservation in exchange for preventing starvation; a queue cannot get \"credit\" beyond what it actually used.\n\n### 4.5 Seat-Request Oversubscription\n\nWhen the head-of-queue request requires more seats than the total `ConcurrencyLimit`, `canAccommodateSeatsLocked` (`queueset.go:748`) blocks dispatch unless the queueset is completely empty (`totRequestsExecuting == 0`). This prevents deadlock (the oversize request would never dispatch if any other request were running), but it can cause the queueset to stall if requests ahead of it are slow to finish.\n\n### 4.6 Configuration Change Without Disruption\n\nQueue count reduction uses attrition: queues are only removed when they drain naturally (`removeQueueIfEmptyLocked`). Queue count increase is immediate (`setConfiguration` appends new queues). This means a reduction takes time proportional to the slowest current request, and in the interim the old queues continue to be considered for dispatch, slightly diluting the new configuration.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Risks\n\n### 5.1 `QueueSetFactory` / `promiseFactoryFactory`\n\nThe public factory is `NewQueueSetFactory(c eventclock.Interface)` (`queueset.go:170`). Tests can substitute `newTestableQueueSetFactory` with a custom `promiseFactoryFactory`. The `promiseFactory` type is `func(initial interface{}, doneCtx context.Context, doneVal interface{}) promise.WriteOnce`. This is the only hook that changes locking semantics \u2014 a wrong implementation here can deadlock (if `Set` blocks while the lock is held) or cause data races (if `Get` is called under the lock).\n\n### 5.2 `WorkEstimatorFunc`\n\n**File:** `request/width.go:89`\n\nThe work estimator is pluggable via `WorkEstimatorFunc`. Three estimators are composed: list (object-count based), mutating (watch-count based), and a default (1 seat). Operators can influence behavior by adjusting `WorkEstimatorConfig` fields such as `MinimumSeats`, `MaximumListSeatsLimit`, and `MaximumMutatingSeatsLimit`. Misconfiguring these can cause either underestimation (allowing too many heavy requests through) or overestimation (starving legitimate traffic).\n\n### 5.3 Borrowing Adjustment via `updateBorrowing`\n\n**File:** `apf_controller.go:393`\n\nThe borrowing loop runs every `borrowingAdjustmentPeriod` (10 seconds) and calls `computeConcurrencyAllocation` to solve a bounded allocation problem. Each priority level has `[minCL, maxCL]` bounds and a `target` derived from smoothed demand. The smoothing coefficient `seatDemandSmoothingCoefficient = 0.977` gives a half-life of approximately 5 minutes. Operators can indirectly tune this by adjusting `lendablePercent` and `borrowingLimitPercent` in `PriorityLevelConfiguration`. Setting `lendablePercent = 0` makes a level non-lendable (it always holds its nominal allocation); setting `borrowingLimitPercent = nil` allows unlimited borrowing up to `serverConcurrencyLimit`.\n\nRisk: the borrowing algorithm converges every 10 seconds. A sustained burst that lasts under 10 seconds and then subsides does not trigger reborrowing back, because `seatDemandStats.smoothed` decays slowly. In practice this means transiently busy levels hold borrowed capacity for minutes after the burst ends.\n\n### 5.4 `QueueNoteFn`\n\n`StartRequest` accepts a `QueueNoteFn fq.QueueNoteFn` callback that is invoked with `true` when the request enters a queue and `false` when it leaves (either dispatched or rejected). This is used by `apf_filter.go` to track `startWaitingTime` for queue wait latency metrics and for `httplog.AddKeyValue`.\n\n### 5.5 Mandatory FlowSchemas and Priority Levels\n\n`configController` ensures the `exempt` and `catch-all` FlowSchemas and PriorityLevelConfigurations always exist, creating imagined stand-ins with `imaginePL` if the API objects are missing. The catch-all priority level uses `DesiredNumQueues > 0` by the default mandatory config, so unauthenticated or misclassified traffic is queued rather than rejected outright \u2014 a safety mechanism that also means the catch-all level can become a congestion point.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance\n\nThe `sync.Mutex` in `queueSet` serializes all state changes, including `StartRequest`, `Finish`, and every `EventAfterDuration` callback for lingering seats. At high request rates this mutex can become a bottleneck. Each priority level has its own QueueSet with its own lock, so the contention is scoped to a single priority level.\n\nThe `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` loop runs `O(queues)` iterations per request arrival and per request completion. With 128 queues (the default `WorkloadDefault` configuration) this is 128 iterations for each event. At 1000 requests/second per priority level and 128 queues, the dispatch loop runs ~128,000 iterations/second \u2014 negligible CPU, but it does hold the lock throughout.\n\nThe `syncTimeLocked` call at every lock acquisition computes `getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()` which itself iterates over all queues to sum seat demand. This is another `O(queues)` scan per lock acquisition.\n\n### 6.2 Reliability\n\nThe `promise.WriteOnce` design ensures that `Finish()` never returns while `execFn()` is still running, even if the context is cancelled. This is guaranteed by the deferred structure in `Finish` (`queueset.go:386`): cancellation can only be observed after `wait()` returns, and if `wait()` returned `exec=true` then `execFn` runs to completion before `finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible` is called.\n\nLingering seat release via `EventAfterDuration` spawns a goroutine per request with `FinalSeats > 0`. If the API server is under heavy load with many watch completions, these goroutines pile up. Each one re-acquires the QueueSet lock, so they serialize correctly, but the goroutine creation is not bounded beyond the total executing request count.\n\n### 6.3 Maintainability\n\nThe two-level locking structure (outer `configController.lock sync.RWMutex` and inner per-QueueSet `sync.Mutex`) is documented but requires care: `startRequest` holds a read lock on the controller while calling into the QueueSet, which holds its own lock. The `Handle \u2192 startRequest \u2192 QueueSet.StartRequest` call chain spans both locks. Extending this with additional blocking inside `StartRequest` (e.g., a third data structure lock) risks deadlock.\n\nThe virtual time epoch advancement (`advanceEpoch`) mutates every queue and every waiting request's `arrivalR`. This O(requests \u00d7 queues) operation runs while the lock is held. In a pathological scenario with thousands of queued requests, this could stall dispatch for a measurable period.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Critical Files and Directories\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go` | Public interface: `QueueSetFactory`, `QueueSet`, `Request`, `QueuingConfig`, `DispatchingConfig` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go` | Core FQSR implementation: virtual time, dispatch loop, enqueue, finish |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go` | Data structures: `request`, `queue`, `completedWorkEstimate`, `queueSum` |\n| # Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive

## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies

The API Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet subsystem is the engine that enforces concurrency limits and inter-flow fairness for the Kubernetes apiserver. Its responsibilities are narrowly scoped: given a request already classified into a priority level, the QueueSet decides whether to execute it immediately, queue it until capacity becomes available, or reject it entirely.

**What it is not responsible for:**

- Classification of requests to priority levels or flow schemas — that belongs to `configController.startRequest()` in `apf_controller.go`.
- The admission webhook pipeline, authentication, or authorization.
- Scheduling of the work itself — it dispatches a signal; the actual handler runs in the caller's goroutine.

**Upstream dependencies (inputs to the QueueSet):**

- `configController` (`apf_controller.go`) supplies `QueuingConfig` (number of queues, queue depth, hand size) and `DispatchingConfig` (concurrency limit) through the two-phase construction API.
- `WorkEstimate` (`request/width.go`) carries the work model: `InitialSeats`, `FinalSeats`, and `AdditionalLatency`.
- `shufflesharding.Dealer` (`util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go`) provides the queue-selection algorithm.
- `eventclock.Interface` (`fairqueuing/eventclock/`) is the monotonic time source used for virtual-time accounting.

**Downstream dependencies (what the QueueSet hands off to):**

- `apf_filter.go` receives the `fq.Request` object and calls `Finish(execFn)`, which blocks until the QueueSet dispatches or rejects the request.
- `metrics` package (`flowcontrol/metrics/`) is updated at every state change: enqueue, dequeue, dispatch, reject, cancel.
- `promise.WriteOnce` (`fairqueuing/
... (truncated)
